    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="93daacde4ffc4774912fa2f72cba0826">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: '7aeaab60-d0d8-4699-bd1a-9cac1cbf7130'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Feng/Xiangming">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Cao/Yuliang" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a8" data-db-target-for="a8" aria-controls="a8" aria-haspopup="true" id="a8_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Yuliang Cao<i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-mail_outline"></i></span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a8" aria-labelledby="a8_Ctrl" role="region" id="a8">
                     <p class="author-type mb-1">Corresponding Author</p>
                     <p class="author-name">Yuliang Cao</p>
                     <ul class="rlist sm-account">
                        <li class="sm-account__item"><a class="sm-account__link" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:ylcao@whu.edu.cn"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-ic_mail_solid"></i><span>ylcao@whu.edu.cn</span></a></li>
                     </ul>
                     <p>Hubei Key Laboratory of Electrochemical Power Sources, College of Chemistry and Molecular Science, Wuhan University, Wuhan, 430072 P. R. China</p>E-mail: <a class="corr-email" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:chenweih@zzu.edu.cn"><span>chenweih@zzu.edu.cn</span></a>, <a class="corr-email" title="Link to email address" href="mailto:ylcao@whu.edu.cn"><span>ylcao@whu.edu.cn</span></a><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Cao/Yuliang">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Shen/Changyu" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a9" data-db-target-for="a9" aria-controls="a9" aria-haspopup="true" id="a9_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Changyu Shen</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a9" aria-labelledby="a9_Ctrl" role="region" id="a9">
                     <p class="author-name">Changyu Shen</p>
                     <p>National Engineering and Research Center for Advanced Polymer Processing Technology, Zhengzhou University, Zhengzhou, 450001 P. R. China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Shen/Changyu">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span></div>

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d33333249" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have gained tremendous interest for grid scale energy storage system and power energy batteries. However, the current researches of anode for SIBs still face the critical issues of low areal capacity, limited cycle life, and low initial coulombic efficiency for practical application perspective. To solve this issue, a kind of hierarchical 3D carbon-networks/Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/graphene (CFG) is designed and synthesized as freestanding anode, which is constructed with Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> microparticles well-welded on 3D-crosslinked carbon-networks and embedded in highly conductive graphene film, via a facile and scalable synthetic method. The as-prepared freestanding electrode CFG represents high areal capacity (2.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.25 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) and excellent cycle stability of 5000 cycles (0.0095% capacity decay per cycle). The assembled all-flexible sodium-ion battery delivers remarkable performance (high areal capacity of 1.42 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.3 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> and superior energy density of 144 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>), which are very close to the requirement of practical application. This work not only enlightens the material design and electrode engineering, but also provides a new kind of freestanding high energy density anode with great potential application prospective for SIBs.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma201806664-sec-0010">
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have garnered considerable attention for most promising stationary energy storage system and show potential application on power energy batteries, by virtue of the rich nature abundance of sodium and similar energy storage mechanism with lithium-ion batteries.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0001_R_d33333231e509" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Science Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Nat. Mater. Chem. Rev.">1</a></span> In recent years, with the increasing researches of SIBs, the urgent demands for SIBs with high energy density and cycle stability is overwhelmingly emerging.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0002_R_d33333231e511" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Nat. Energy">2</a></span> Some works for cathode materials, such as layered transition metal oxides, polyanionic compounds, and Prussian blue analogs, have shown encouraging research status.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0003_R_d33333231e513" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Adv. Energy Mater. Chem. Soc. Rev. Joule">3</a></span> While, for anode, large challenges and barriers still exist for finding suitable electrode materials in term of high capacity, high cycle stability as well as high initial coulombic efficiency (ICE).</p>
         
         <p>For anode materials, carbonaceous materials (hard carbons, expanded graphite, and graphene),<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0004_R_d33333231e518" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Energy Mater.">4</a></span> alloy-based materials,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0005_R_d33333231e520" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem Nat. Nanotechnol.">5</a></span> organic compounds,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0006_R_d33333231e522" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Energy Mater.">6</a></span> and metal oxides/sulfides<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0007_R_d33333231e524" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Adv. Energy Mater. Adv. Mater. Nat. Commun.">7</a></span> have been widely discovered and investigated for SIBs. Carbonaceous materials, considered as the most promising anode materials, own the favorable low operating voltage and cycle stability, however, low rate performance, low capacity as well as safety concerns for sodium metal plating at high polarization condition, which seriously limited its practical application.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0008_R_d33333231e526" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater. J. Am. Chem. Soc.">8</a></span> The alloy-based materials show superior high capacity (400–2600 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) but are impeded by huge volume expansion (126–520%) derived limited cycle life.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0009_R_d33333231e531" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Adv. Mater. J. Am. Chem. Soc.">9</a></span> Organic compounds exhibit the advantage of structural designability but disadvantages of solubility in electrolyte and low conductivity.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0006_R_d33333231e533" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Energy Mater.">6</a></span> Metal oxide/sulfide materials based on conversion reaction have received significant attentions due to their high theoretical capacity, rich reservation, and intrinsic safety.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0010_R_d33333231e535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Energy Mater.">10</a></span> However, these conversion materials also suffer from large volume changes, multiphase transformation, and slow kinetics that lead to the poor rate performance and unsatisfactory cycle stability. In these materials, metal sulfides (MS<i><sub>x</sub></i>, M = Fe,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0011_R_d33333231e540" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a></span> Sn,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0012_R_d33333231e543" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Energy Environ. Sci. Joule">12</a></span> Mo,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0013" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0013_R_d33333231e545" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 13 - ACS Nano">13</a></span> Co,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0014_R_d33333231e547" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Nano Energy">14</a></span> Ni,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0015_R_d33333231e549" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Nano">15</a></span> etc.) have possess industrial prospective owing to the improved reversibility compared with metal oxides.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0016_R_d33333231e551" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Mater.">16</a></span></p>
         
         <p>Among metal sulfides, iron sulfides with the nature of abundant resources, cost-effectiveness, and environmental compatibility, fulfill the major criteria for the applications.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0017_R_d33333231e555" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Nat. Commun.">17</a></span> In addition, iron sulfides with different sulfur contents exhibit distinguished electrochemical characteristics, such as specific capacity and charge–discharge voltage plateaus.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0018_R_d33333231e557" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Chem. Sci. Small">18</a></span> And strategies have been proposed to mitigate the problems include controlling the cut-off voltage,[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0011_R_d33333231e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0018_R_d33333231e559" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Chem. Sci. Small">18</a></span>] nanostructures construction[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0018_R_d33333231e562" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Chem. Sci. Small">18</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0019_R_d33333231e562" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - ACS Nano">19</a></span>] and carbon coating.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0020_R_d33333231e565" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">20</a></span> Chen's group<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0011_R_d33333231e568" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a></span> stabled the FeS<sub>2</sub> material for 20 000 cycles by controlling the cut-off voltage to 0.8 V, but this method extremely sacrifices the specific capacity (only 250 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and highly raises the operation voltage. Wang et al.[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0020_R_d33333231e574" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">20</a></span>] synthesized FeS@Fe<sub>3</sub>C@GC composite with 3D interconnected structure, which shows high capacity over 700 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> but more than 20% capacity decay after 100 cycles. Consequently, these strategies always cannot satisfy the capacity, ICE, cycle life, power characteristic, and large-scale synthesis method simultaneously.</p>
         
         <p>Additionally, another essential aspect, areal capacity (2–3 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> for today's Li-ion batteries),<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0021_R_d33333231e586" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - J. Electrochem. Soc. Nat. Energy">21</a></span> is very important for commercial application. But current research on promotion for areal capacity of anode materials for SIBs is just limited in a low value (&lt;0.5 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>),<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0022_R_d33333231e590" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Mater.">22</a></span> which is because that thicker electrode would cause high polarization and electrode crack, leading to low capacity and poor cycling performance. Furthermore, in commonly slurry-casting electrode, nonactive materials (including additional conductive agent, insulating binder, and metal current collector) occupy most of the weight (≈85–90 wt%), which significantly reduces the energy density of the whole electrode. Freestanding electrode with binder free property could effectively provide higher energy density by avoiding the additional non-active materials in electrodes.[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0005_R_d33333231e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Chem Nat. Nanotechnol.">5</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0023_R_d33333231e592" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Science">23</a></span>] Meanwhile, freestanding property can realize the flexibility of electrode. As the growing demands of flexible electronic devices for flexible energy storage systems,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0024_R_d33333231e596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - Adv. Mater.">24</a></span> consequently, flexible freestanding electrode with high areal mass loading is of excellent prospects for future application.</p>
         
         <p>Herein, we designed and synthesized a flexible freestanding electrode with hierarchical structure, 3D carbon-networks/Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>/graphene (CFG), via a simple and scalable method. The constructed flexible freestanding electrode CFG is composed of a 3D-crosslinked conductive substrate, high-capacity iron sulfides, and high-conductivity graphene coating, and this novel hierarchical structure is firstly reported for anodes of SIBs. The hierarchical structure endows the CFG electrode with excellent electron and ion conductivity along with structural stability, to effectively promote the rate performance and cycle performance of iron sulfides. Significantly, the as-prepared flexible freestanding electrode CFG can possess high areal capacity of 2.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.25 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with a high ICE (81%), high rate performance (1.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 5 C, 1 C corresponds to 2 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>) and excellent long cycle stability (95% capacity retention after 500 cycles and only 0.0095% decay per cycle for 5000 cycles). In addition, the all-flexible pouch-type sodium-ion full cell with flexible freestanding CFG anode, flexible Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C cathode and flexible modified cellulose acetate separator is also attained with high storage performance of 1.42 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> and high energy density of 144 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>, which meet completely the requirement of present application.</p>
         
         <p>The freestanding CFG electrode was synthesized via a facile two-step method including assembling process and thermal treatment, as illustrated in <b>Scheme</b> <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0005">1</a>. The FeS<sub>2</sub> were firstly surface modified by (3-aminopropyl) triethoxysilane (APTES) to obtain surface-aminated positively charged FeS<sub>2</sub> in moderate acidic condition.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0025_R_d33333231e640" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - J. Mater. Chem. A">25</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0026_R_d33333231e640" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">26</a></span> Briefly, the 3D-hierarchical-wrapping structure was managed via the weak chemical interactions between positively-charged FeS<sub>2</sub> microparticles and negatively charged oxygen-containing groups of cotton fibers and graphene oxide (GO) film. The effectively assembling process was successfully triggered out through tailoring the Zeta potential of FeS<sub>2</sub> microparticles (Figure S1, Supporting Information). Finally, the flexible freestanding CFG was obtained after annealing process, during which GO layers were reduced to graphene, cotton textile were carbonized to carbon networks while FeS<sub>2</sub> transformed to Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> simultaneously owing to the inevitable sulfur loss at high temperature. For comparison, carbonized cotton (CC) and carbonized cotton/graphene (CG) were also prepared to clearly interpret the sodium storage performance of the CFG freestanding electrode.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma201806664-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/143266a4-3b92-4d9f-9efe-4f8445fb2c4b/adma201806664-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/143266a4-3b92-4d9f-9efe-4f8445fb2c4b/adma201806664-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/a8839d6e-7b68-46c9-91b3-3781a5d6a40a/adma201806664-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/143266a4-3b92-4d9f-9efe-4f8445fb2c4b/adma201806664-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Scheme 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma201806664-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.201806664" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Schematic illustration of synthetic procedure of freestanding CFG electrode.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Pristine FeS<sub>2</sub> shows the microsphere that composed of nanoparticles in scanning electron microscopy (SEM) characterization (Figure S2a, Supporting Information). The diameter of the fibers in CC (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>a) were obviously shrinking compared to pristine cotton (Figure S2b, Supporting Information) due to the pyrolysis of cellulose in the thermal treatment process. In low magnification image, the flexible freestanding CFG shows a 3D-crosslinked structure with highly homogeneous dispersion of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> microparticles (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>b,c). Moreover, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles were well-welded on the carbon fibers, which can be certified in 3D carbon-networks/Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (CF) composite (Figure S2c, Supporting Information). This loading form could combine the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles with conductive network while avoiding the undesirable aggregation. Benefited from excellent conductivity and high mechanical strength, graphene is considered as one of the most ideal coating materials.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0027_R_d33333231e700" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Adv. Energy Mater. Nat. Mater.">27</a></span> It is found that the extremely thin and firmly coating of graphene wrapping layer in CFG, which is distinctly revealed in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>d,e, implies the well encapsulating of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles. This tightly coating of graphene film, consequently, owns the superb merits of promoting the conductivity of entire electrode, buffering the volume variation and avoiding the abscission of the active material during charging and discharging, which relieves most critical issues of high performance anode materials. As for CG electrode, the same chemical interactions between positively charged APTES and oxygen-containing groups of GO as well as cotton also give rise to tightly coating of graphene films on carbon fibers (Figure S2d, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma201806664-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/73409489-14a8-443f-96a4-d0385630f155/adma201806664-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/73409489-14a8-443f-96a4-d0385630f155/adma201806664-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/f6a07aa0-d84f-4e3f-b6ae-7c4f4689f068/adma201806664-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/73409489-14a8-443f-96a4-d0385630f155/adma201806664-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma201806664-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.201806664" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Structural characterization of flexible freestanding CFG electrode with SEM, XRD, XPS, and Raman. a) SEM of carbonized cotton (inset: digital image of pristine cotton cloth) showing shrank fibers with smooth surfaces and diameter of ≈10 µm. b–d) SEM images of CFG at various magnification depicting the highly homogeneous dispersion of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> microparticles and embedding in graphene film (inset: digital image of twisted CFG). e) Mapping analysis of CFG illustrating the thin coating film of graphene. f) XRD patterns of CFG, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and CG together with XPS spectra of CFG, g) Fe 2p, and h) S 2p confirming the crystal phase of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and hard carbon in CFG. i) Raman analysis of CFG with <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> = 1.2 revealing favorable conductivity of carbon species.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The X-ray diffraction (XRD) peaks of prepared flexible freestanding CFG could be well assigned to Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> (JCPDS No. 76–2308) with a hexagonal phase, in which the peaks at 29.9°, 33.9°, 43.9°, and 53.1° are indexed to (200), (203), (206), and (220) plane, respectively (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>f). The broad peak at around 23° is ascribed to the (002) plane of graphite microcrystals in amorphous carbon,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0004_R_d33333231e751" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Adv. Energy Mater.">4</a></span> which is accordant with XRD pattern of CG. In addition, the crystal Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in CFG was transformed from pristine FeS<sub>2</sub> owing to the inevitable sulfur loss at high temperature, same as Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> sample. As anode for SIBs, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> owns the high theoretical specific capacity of 662 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> (Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> + 16Na<sup>+</sup> + 16e<sup>−</sup> → 7Fe + 8Na<sub>2</sub>S).<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0028_R_d33333231e782" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Mater. Chem. A">28</a></span> And compared with FeS<sub>2</sub>, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> shows lower charge–discharge voltage plateaus,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0029_R_d33333231e790" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Nano Energy">29</a></span> which is highly beneficial for energy densities of full-cells when matched with cathodes. Moreover, the band gap of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is zero, representing high electron conductivity that favorable for the fast kinetics.[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0018_R_d33333231e797" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Chem. Sci. Small">18</a></span>]</p>
         
         <p>The chemical bonding situation of flexible freestanding electrode CFG is studied by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) analysis. XPS spectra in Figure S3a of the Supporting Information shows the presences of Fe, S, C, O, N, and Si elements. In Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>g, the photoelectron peak at 707.9 eV in Fe 2p spectrum indicates the presence of metallic Fe while peaks center at 711.2 and 724.6 eV are attributed to Fe<sup>2+</sup> in CFG. In addition, the peaks at 713.7 and 726.8 eV are related to Fe<sup>3+</sup>,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0030_R_d33333231e809" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Energy Lett.">30</a></span> which may be associated with the surface oxidation of CFG. The photoelectron peaks in S 2p spectrum are corresponded to S<sup>2−</sup> (161.7 and 163.1 eV), S<i><sub>n</sub></i><sup>2−</sup> (163.9 and 165.0 eV) and SO<i><sub>x</sub></i> (168.6 and 169.7 eV), respectively (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>h). The high-resolution spectra of C 1s displays the existence of O<span class="icomoon"></span>CO (289.3 eV), C<span class="icomoon"></span>C (286.2 eV), and CC (284.8 eV) (Figure S3b, Supporting Information). As for O 1s spectrum, the photoelectron binding energy of 530.7, 532.3, and 533.9 eV are related to O<span class="icomoon"></span>H (Si<span class="icomoon"></span>O), C<span class="icomoon"></span>O (Si<span class="icomoon"></span>O<span class="icomoon"></span>Si), and C<span class="icomoon"></span>O<span class="icomoon"></span>C, respectively (Figure S3c, Supporting Information). These peaks verify the successful formation of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and carbon species in CFG material. Carbonization degree of carbon species in CFG is analyzed by Raman spectra test to evaluate the conductivity (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0001">1</a>i). The prominent D-band (at around 1350 cm<sup>−1</sup>) is ascribed to sp<sup>3</sup> carbon atoms in defects or amorphous carbon, while G-band (at around 1590 cm<sup>−1</sup>) is related to ordered structures of sp<sup>2</sup> carbon atoms.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0031_R_d33333231e838" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Chemistry">31</a></span> The <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> ratio, commonly used to evaluate the disordered level of carbon material,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0032_R_d33333231e847" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Adv. Mater.">32</a></span> is fitted and calculated to be 1.2 for CFG electrode (Figure S4, Supporting Information), indicating the well enough conductivity of carbon species. The content of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in CFG is 35.7 wt% proved by thermogravimetric analysis in Figure S5 of the Supporting Information. The areal mass loading of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in CFG electrode is 3 mg cm<sup>−2</sup>.</p>
         
         <p>Cyclic voltammetry (CV) of CFG (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>a) shows accordant peaks' locations with those of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and CG anode (Figure S6a,b, Supporting Information). During initial cathodic scan (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>a), the sharp peak at 0.79 V is related to sodiation process that Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation into both Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> and carbon species,[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0020_R_d33333231e881" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">20</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0033_R_d33333231e881" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Energy Mater.">33</a></span>] along with the decomposition of electrolyte and formation of solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) layers.[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0034_R_d33333231e884" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Nano Energy Energy Environ. Sci. Joule">34</a></span>] This peak is greatly weakened in following cycle due to the irreversibility of SEI formation process. When the cell was discharged to 0.3 V, the sodiation reactants transformed to Na-rich phases and partially formed Fe and Na<sub>2</sub>S via conversion reaction.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0030_R_d33333231e890" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Energy Lett.">30</a></span> After the first cycle, the reduction peaks located at 0.92 V are corresponding to the reaction between Na<sup>+</sup> and Na<sub>2−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub>. As for charging process, the oxidation peaks at 1.38 V are correlated to the desodiation process with generation of Na<sub>2−</sub><i><sub>x</sub></i>FeS<sub>2</sub>.[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0020_R_d33333231e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">20</a></span>] The CV profiles of CF show the same redox peaks' locations except that the peak strength is obviously decreased (Figure S6c, Supporting Information). Considering the same scan rate, the elevation of redox current strength of CFG is attributed to the capacity promotion due to the higher conductivity aroused by the advantageous hierarchical structure. The corresponding CV profiles of CG and CC illustrate low contributions of carbon species for sodium storage capacity in CFG electrode (Figure S6b,d, Supporting Information).</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma201806664-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4f704b43-ac71-49c3-9e4c-a8408eaa0fa1/adma201806664-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/4f704b43-ac71-49c3-9e4c-a8408eaa0fa1/adma201806664-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/3cd4ae2f-787e-419a-a0b7-3550e10f8205/adma201806664-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4f704b43-ac71-49c3-9e4c-a8408eaa0fa1/adma201806664-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma201806664-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.201806664" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical sodium storage performance of flexible freestanding CFG electrode in half-cell. a) Cyclic voltammetry (CV) profiles for initial 2 cycles at scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>−1</sup>. b) Charge–discharge profiles for initial 2 cycles at 0.25 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>. c) Rate performance and corresponding d) charge–discharge profiles. e) Cycling performance at high current density of 6 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>, showing 0.0095% capacity decay per cycle after 5000 cycles. The comparison of areal capacity for CFG electrode with various recently reported f) high performance freestanding anodes and g) high performance iron sulfides materials for SIBs.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>To further evaluate the electrochemical performance of flexible freestanding CFG as anode for SIBs, galvanostatic tests were performed via coin-type half-cells. To distinctly and reasonably reveal the differences between the as-prepared materials, and figure out the contribution and impact of each component, the test results are determined in areal capacity (mAh cm<sup>−2</sup>), which is an important parameter for practical application. For charge–discharge profiles of CFG in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>b, the long and flat discharge plateau in the first cycle is corresponding to the sodiation process and the SEI formation process, which could be clearly seen in differential charge–discharge capacity curves versus voltage (Figure S7, Supporting Information), accordant with the CV profiles. The initial discharge and charge areal capacities were 2.62 and 2.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> with the corresponding ICE of 81%, while the capacity loss was attributed to the irreversible formation of SEI film and partial irreversible sodiation/desodiation process in the first cycle. The areal capacity and ICE are much higher than most reported anode materials for SIBs (Tables S1 and S2, Supporting Information) and owns superiority for the practical application. The high ICE is attributed to the relatively higher reversibility of the sodiation/desodiation process, as well as fewer consumption of electrolyte for SEI formation, owing to the lower specific area of microsized Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> particles and thinner SEI film benefited from the precisely graphene coating.[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0034_R_d33333231e946" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Nano Energy Energy Environ. Sci. Joule">34</a></span>] The flexible freestanding CFG electrode delivers reversible areal capacity of 2.12, 2.08, 2.03, 1.84, 1.66, 1.46, and 1.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at current densities of 0.25, 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 4.0, 6.0, and 10.0 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> (1 C corresponds to 2 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>), respectively in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>c. The correspondent charge–discharge curves are displayed in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>d. The differential charge–discharge capacity curves versus voltage of CFG, Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, and CG at different current density (Figure S8, Supporting Information) shows that Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> makes the predominant contribution to the capacity of CFG electrode at high rates. This was attributed to the intercalation reaction of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> with fast kinetics at higher voltage, instead of the conversion reaction with sluggish kinetics at lower voltage.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0011_R_d33333231e973" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a></span> In addition, the excellent rate performance is owing to its hierarchical structure, that the Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> microparticles distribute on 3D-crosslinked carbon networks and coated with graphene film, so that the high dispersion, high conductivity, and high wetting characteristic with electrolyte (proved via contact angle test in Figure S9, Supporting Information) is successfully achieved.</p>
         
         <p>To study the performance of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> in CFG, the specific capacity of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> is calculated to be 536 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.08 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure S10, Supporting Information), based on the analysis of capacity for CG anode (Figure S11a, Supporting Information), showing the excellent capacity representation of iron sulfides in the hierarchical CFG. The cycle performance test of CFG, performed at high current density of 6 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>e), shows excellent stability and superior reversibility with 95% capacity retention after 500 cycles and only 0.0095% decay per cycle over 5000 cycles. The charge–discharge curves in different cycles shown in Figure S12 of the Supporting Information demonstrate well-retain of the sodium storage characteristics of flexible freestanding CFG electrode. For comparison, the CF electrode without graphene coating shows rapidly capacity decay during cycling, confirming effectively cycle stability promotion with the coating of graphene layer in CFG.</p>
         
         <p>The synergistic effect of hierarchical structure and multilevel conductive components plays a major role for the remarkable performance of CFG, which combining high-capacity Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> microparticles with fast kinetics, high-conductive 3D carbon-networks, and tightly wrapping of graphene layer. When compared with various recently reported high performance freestanding anodes (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>f;<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0035_R_d33333231e1008" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Adv. Mater. Adv. Mater. Adv. Funct. Mater. Nano Energy Carbon Nat. Commun.">35</a></span> Table S1, Supporting Information) and high performance iron sulfides materials (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0002">2</a>g;[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0018_R_d33333231e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed. Chem. Sci. Small">18</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0020_R_d33333231e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Adv. Funct. Mater. ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">20</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0029_R_d33333231e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Nano Energy">29</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0030_R_d33333231e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Energy Lett.">30</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0034_R_d33333231e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Nano Energy Energy Environ. Sci. Joule">34</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0036_R_d33333231e1013" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Energy Environ. Sci.">36</a></span>] Table S2, Supporting Information) for SIBs, the present flexible freestanding CFG anode represents high areal capacity, superior rate performance, and excellent long cycle life. Consequently, the flexible freestanding anode CFG with high areal capacity and cycle stability shows great superiority for the actual commercial application.</p>
         
         <div class="paragraph-element">The <i>operando</i> XRD was performed to further investigate the sodium storage mechanism of flexible freestanding electrode CFG (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0003">3</a>a). It is obvious that the densities of two peaks of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, which located at 29.9° and 33.9°, decreased during the discharge process in the first cycle, which means the main phase of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> had participated in the sodiation reaction. Notably, the peak at 29.9 °C shifted to lower angles in sodiation process and turned back to higher angles in desodiation process. This confirms the small lattice spacing expansion and contraction of partial sodiation product Na<sub>3</sub>(FeS<sub>2</sub>)<sub>2</sub>,<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0037_R_d33333231e1041" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J. Solid State Chem.">37</a></span> caused by the insertion and extraction of sodium ions. Nevertheless, this peak did not return to its initial position in the charge state, indicating the reaction could not back to Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> phase, which is accordant with the disappearance of peak at 33.9°. The peak of intermediate product Na<sub>2</sub>FeS<sub>2</sub> at 26.9° is also detected in discharge process of first cycle.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0037_R_d33333231e1052" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - J. Solid State Chem.">37</a></span> These findings elucidate the intercalation reaction mechanism of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> during initial cycling. As the products of conversion reaction, the peaks of Na<sub>2</sub>S (42.3°) and Fe (43.1°) gradually emerged in the first discharge process and stayed exist in the following process.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0030_R_d33333231e1061" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - ACS Energy Lett.">30</a></span> Considering the previous analysis of CV profiles and differential capacity curves, the charge–discharge reaction mechanism of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> can be described as follows<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0011_R_d33333231e1067" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Energy Environ. Sci.">11</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0017_R_d33333231e1067" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Nat. Commun.">17</a>, <a href="#adma201806664-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0028_R_d33333231e1067" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - J. Mater. Chem. A">28</a></span><div class="inline-equation" id="adma201806664-disp-0001"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE--><span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/5648579b-4401-49d7-be12-9c308669cd34/adma201806664-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:dummy:media:adma201806664:adma201806664-math-0001" display="block" location="graphic/adma201806664-math-0001.png">

         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma201806664-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/c83d6e1e-5e4b-49b2-8e80-d7d984430ce7/adma201806664-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/c83d6e1e-5e4b-49b2-8e80-d7d984430ce7/adma201806664-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/5ee0876e-a954-46c2-8533-27b55a2c5a29/adma201806664-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/c83d6e1e-5e4b-49b2-8e80-d7d984430ce7/adma201806664-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma201806664-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.201806664" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Sodium storage mechanism analysis of CFG. a) <i>Operando</i> XRD analysis of the sodium storage mechanism of CFG for the initial 3 cycles. Narrow 2θ windows are shown here for clarify. b) Schematic illustration of sodium storage mechanism of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, depicting intercalation reaction combined with conversion reaction. c) Morphology evolution of CFG and CF electrode after 3 cycles, illustrating the favorable structure stability of hierarchical CFG electrode.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The corresponding schematic illustration of sodium storage mechanism shown in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0003">3</a>b depicts the intercalation reaction combined with conversion reaction for charge–discharge process of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>.</p>
         
         <p>The morphology evolution of the CFG recorded by SEM after 3 cycles in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0003">3</a>c, shows microparticle of Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> maintained well and no noticeable particle broken can be found. While without graphene coating, CF electrode shows obviously breakage after 3 cycles. Furthermore, the morphologies of CFG and CF after 2000 cycles also demonstrate the same results (Figure S13, Supporting Information). This proves that the graphene wrapping layer could effectively relieve the expansion/contraction stress and preserve the structure stability during the sodiation/desodiation process. Owing to the conversion reaction mechanism with discharge product of Na<sub>2</sub>S, the iron sulfides suffer from the possibility of sulfur species' loss, especially in a wide potential window. Consequently, the stability of sulfur species of freestanding CFG in wide potential window is really a key impact factor for the long cycle performance. To investigate this issue, the energy dispersive X-ray element spectrometry (EDS) analysis of freestanding CFG and CF electrode after 2000 cycles is performed, which is shown in Figure S14 of the Supporting Information. The higher atomic percentage ratio of S and Fe elements in freestanding CFG electrode, indicates fewer sulfur loss with graphene wrapping layers. This post cycling analysis reveals the hierarchical structure of freestanding CFG composite could effectively alleviate the loss of sulfur content in the process of cycling, which is extremely benefited for the long cycle stability of the electrode. Moreover, the Nyquist plots of CFG and CF electrodes measured at 0.3 V in the first cycle show two overlapped semicircles in high-medium frequency and a diagonal line in low frequency (Figure S15a, Supporting Information). The semicircle in high-medium frequency is related to the characteristic of SEI on the surfaces of the electrodes.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0038_R_d33333231e1336" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - ACS Nano">38</a></span> The semicircle in medium frequency region indicates the faradaic impedance of charge transport process, while the diagonal line in low frequency is related to the mass transport impedance of Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in active material.<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0022_R_d33333231e1341" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Adv. Mater.">22</a></span> The Nyquist plots was fitted by an equivalent circuit (the inserted image in Figure S15a, Supporting Information). Corresponding to the detailed fitted values of different elements (Table S3, Supporting Information), the CFG electrode shows lower <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and lower <i>R</i><sub>1</sub> compared with CF<sub>,</sub> which indicates the lower resistances of SEI film and charge transfer impedance. For the mass transport properties, accordant with the linear relationship of <i>Z</i>′ and ω<sup>−1/2</sup> in Figure S15b of the Supporting Information, the closely slopes indicate the similar sodium ion diffusion coefficient of CFG and CF electrode. The electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) analysis shows the freestanding CFG anode owns lower interface impedance owing to the thin and stable SEI film derived from the graphene coating layers,[<span><a href="#adma201806664-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma201806664-bib-0034_R_d33333231e1356" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Nano Energy Energy Environ. Sci. Joule">34</a></span>] which greatly contributes to the superior rate performance. The postcycling analysis illustrates the excellent performance of freestanding CFG is attributed to the structural stability, composition stability, and interface stability benefited from the 3D carbon-networks and precisely coating of graphene layers.</p>
         
         <p>For the actual application of the as-prepared material, flexible pouch-type full cell is necessary to be designed and investigated. As example, flexible Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C (abbreviated as NVP@C) was selected as cathode to match with flexible freestanding CFG anode. Considering the electrochemical window (Figure S16, Supporting Information) and compatibilities with electrodes, NaClO<sub>4</sub>/diglyme electrolyte is selected for full cell fabrication. The NVP@C cathode shows a couple of sharp redox peaks in CV profiles (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0004">4</a>c), corresponding to the flat charge–discharge plateaus at ≈3.4 V with high reversible specific capacity of 110 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 C (1 C = 117 mA g<sup>−1</sup>, Figure S17, Supporting Information). The CFG anode shows a major anodic peak (1.4 V) and several cathodic peaks related to the multielectrons reaction. The all-flexible sodium-ion battery is assembled as the schematic illustration in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0004">4</a>a with both flexible electrodes and flexible modified cellulose acetate separator. The charge–discharge plateaus of the full-cell (Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0004">4</a>d) are accordant with the previous analysis of half-cells, with discharge medium voltage is ≈2.0 V, indicating that the low sodium storage voltage of CFG is favorable for achieving high operation voltage of SIBs. An areal capacity of 1.42 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> can be delivered at current density of 0.3 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with high energy density of 144 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total mass of active materials in both electrodes) and stable cycling (0.90 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> after 50 cycles) are reached, and the corresponding coulombic efficiencies are shown in Figure S18 of the Supporting Information. In addition, when both electrodes are preactivated to preform the stable and effective SEI films, the as-fabricated all flexible sodium-ion battery shows high ICE of 96%, higher areal capacity (1.81 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.3 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) and stable cycling performance as shown in Figure S19 of the Supporting Information. The all-flexible sodium-ion battery can light up five light-emitting diode (LED) bulbs in Figure <a href="#adma201806664-fig-0004">4</a>b even under curving condition, showing excellent feasibility for practical use. The superior electrochemical performance of the all-flexible sodium-ion battery shows competitive merits and great prospects for commercial applications.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adma201806664-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/cebf0b36-f23a-4fe8-b2c1-e598147d069e/adma201806664-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/cebf0b36-f23a-4fe8-b2c1-e598147d069e/adma201806664-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/85659571-11ab-48f5-85be-e1372c4a4b12/adma201806664-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/cebf0b36-f23a-4fe8-b2c1-e598147d069e/adma201806664-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma201806664-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.201806664" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical characterization of all-flexible sodium-ion full cell. a) Schematic illustration of the structure of pouch-type full cell depicting both flexible electrodes and flexible separator (inset: digital image of the cell). b) The photo of the pouch-type full cell lighting up LED bulbs for practical use. c) Cyclic voltammetry profiles of flexible Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>@C cathode and CFG anode. d) Charge–discharge profiles of the all-flexible sodium-ion battery in voltage range of 0.3–3.2 V (vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) shows high areal capacity of 1.42 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> and high energy density of 144 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>In summary, we designed and prepared a flexible freestanding CFG electrode with hierarchical structure, in which Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub> microparticles dispersed on 3D-crosslinked flexible conductive substrate, and tightly coating with high conductive graphene film, via a simple and scalable synthesis method. The synergistic effect of hierarchical structure endows CFG with superb merits of adequate electrons and ions transport channels, excellent structural stability along with favorable interface property, which effectively realizes the high rate performance and superior cycle performance of CFG electrode. The as-prepared flexible freestanding CFG electrode delivers high areal capacity of 2.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 0.25 mA cm<sup>−2</sup> with high ICE of 81%, high rate performance (1.12 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> at 10 mA cm<sup>−2</sup>) and excellent long cycle stability for 5000 cycles with only 0.0095% decay per cycle, which are very close to the requirement of practical application. <i>Operando</i> XRD analysis confirmed the combined intercalation and conversion mechanisms with Fe<sub>7</sub>S<sub>8</sub>, which boosts the high capacity and favorable rate performance of CFG. Moreover, the all-flexible sodium-ion battery is also attained with high areal capacity of 1.42 mAh cm<sup>−2</sup> and high energy density of 144 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total mass of active materials in both electrodes). Therefore, the remarkable performance of flexible freestanding CFG electrode possesses superb perspective on future industrial application. Moreover, the electrode engineering and material design in this work can pave the new way for high-performance anode for SIBs directly toward the viably commercial use.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
